Traffic Scam

 

Online advertising fraud continues to be a topic of discussion, and Adweek has named six companies that consistently come up when talking about traffic fraud: AdOn, Adknowledge, eZanga, Jema Media, MGID and BlueLink Marketing. Adweek's Mike Shields covers it: "'AdOn is just about the worst,' said one publisher victimized by bots. 'They are notorious for having the worst quality traffic in the industry,' said another publisher." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iq-B05jDa3oYGBId1s_SEYgb9vCdOcS3Bk7zXOQYjoxEoAgIsI4O6NpjPKUnG78pR_n2asADB44hxxn3rjjX6Okyzl0stex4zQ7CtHRzswQ-QUqT7wpyxRa31djqliIc3fr8fYm4APUrV6YP_eFf5V223TlaZl1f5I3OZQ4w94CJUlMRJsDIIrbpq1zG5JPZHGt-B_1b9lvcOYq8JFfwQjfoav1vdQPrSZp852AsYFo=> .

 

Marketing Native

 

A few weeks after selling NetShelter to Ziff Davis, the brothers behind "native" ads platform InPowered talked to TechCrunch about what they see next for their company. Although InPowered says it has largely been about technology since the platform launched in 2011 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iq-B05jDa3pYsQ-rAI0FNKL4Tcj5QTOB7MusQenGiXb2gJy-DWF7Wxr8b0H9PfPDYB62pW_Q6vpKxNdz9Fy6T4QfgrQ35KBu8m21ANyp8192b7TVM0YZDIE6txgeemeEcxN-jxoGflq71KiDNiGqwvNkj42dLBe6jn_Na-xsGN-ImPkVCbSiTYD3iQTd80zHjw12xOvtkp46MGFNY-bXZvTiL_kiBWj222CCsqRFG6p9EAs74FS7QrhmsxZWgnmPxbmeUbwsk7SEPXXQl5u61mRiJF4BgxGY> , Peyman and Pirouz Nilforoush say the next step is using the money from the sale to promote (i.e. invest in sales and marketing). In case you missed it, instead of focusing on the traditional native advertising model, which turns ads into content, the self-serve InPowered platform allows companies to cherry-pick pre-existing consumer content to turn into ads. Read more on TechCrunch <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iq-B05jDa3qwTnPsoVNI23_sBUeYOe1ssunSNNENgQm98K_gp_OpdlzDnzq32UMrc9Qg1l6yOy7w_B8omyQyNBXCVYJC-nBCvGH1MMqFTs_uuedGUilfoaMF1tQWsPD1J_WebFMTszZuu_agRK_BffGZ02xUweKztO11qCI-mEM=> . InPowered is a classic case of a startup "pivot," where the strategy changes to capitalize on a new market opportunity - native ads online, in this case.

 

Make Silicon Valley Beautiful

 

According to Ad Age, demand for designers is increasing in tech-centric Silicon Valley, as users opt for beautiful products as well as functional ones. "It's important to realize that designers in general have elevated themselves to being equivalent to engineers," said Shannon Callahan, an Andreessen Horowitz partner. Ad Age also points specifically at Google as an example of a company which has recently attempted beautification of their products while trying to attract design talent rather than just engineering talent. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iq-B05jDa3p_wXhgvopIWKJGdt0jMBb8tRBt4ulHVI342GpJnJmK4BsUFKs3EKyyvDKS351sGQrvFIFxFhy9SSu-8PrwNew9NT4xaP5tUxtvfdsUwna8BhOVvpTFMOEQND8mVgUWKxWxBPiFC2h9aXakPLene2xYUKbfl_5cpLpBeLA_gWoBjeBBPUypz9kvzAd6RvWLLt7gk2FlS1luvQ==> .

 

TV Bridge

 

Real Media Group announced a new product - INFUSETV - which will allow advertisers to reach TV audiences on different devices. "INFUSETV provides marketers with the ability to leverage set-top box data and Nielsen GRP measurement tools to complement their existing TV buys," said Nicolle Pangis, President, Real Media Group. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iq-B05jDa3oFBXjtYVImzsyS_Wd-BizPtl07l4mU1ZHY-Lr_xDrFLjkL1GtpopCq9SI3RI-kcFeScBn5fStMHWsq-pt3klm8k6T3GXiLP6SrsoQ2xU778T-H1bX743sqqT1-qmebvL4c3_eoxisLWRIKPgHKEx7ozoy6SGsOB7I=> .

 

IAB Cranks 'Em Out

 

The IAB has released a couple of studies and a display advertising guideline <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iq-B05jDa3rA0HfswgMBvyIDMbaEQVQ3m7e85kPc8gSKlFR4S6SfZPosctCBWQ2FKZcQ0sTutGA-MyU_2E5ob-h_lA55EQ0Gl6AtMTdt0kXvg4w29IEJNOIJLXoTqkJXR_QNfjQ5qyY=> . The Mobile Rising Stars Ad Interaction  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iq-B05jDa3rn6zNOaf6zX6boWojUBS_lGtQhCch7Rf3M6Z97FJEZPg0J6d9zBp7dthukh1FuZlucXjMMBwTI9w5XClErwq2C8Bpj5AkDAfMf4FoBlaB8Y32NoW2cpbPYMJ0ANd-WF_k=> & Effectiveness Study examines the effectiveness of using IAB Mobile Rising Stars creative ad units versus traditional mobile ad units. Their whitepaper Omnichannel and the Drive For Audience Engagement <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iq-B05jDa3rt3oeF3g871eD-GicgEEM6fArc3qMHXU2ohkhZ1oL6UYMqD1LSBo-v1xVzVgUdVRVNqw6ZS1ZVq_xVv_dlUXxi4KlJE9kAn_gKW8FQ1WV2ZFbmS3gn4StK>  explores the changing landscape of advertising including the continually fragmented online audience.

New Mobile Ad Unit

 

Time Inc. is currently testing a new mobile ad unit called Double Snap. The unit consists of a banner that follows users as they scroll, which opens up into a larger ad that doesn't completely obscure content, and then shrinks back to a banner. "It never overlays the content, never takes you away from the content," Solomon Masch, Director of Mobile Sales and Strategy at Time Inc. told Adweek. It's "impossible to miss," he added. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iq-B05jDa3p_oz1RwmJT9Wtf8NiQRk00mdu065UyRu0ucA4x0ZwMiJPPdMEo21SS8lbAnQ8-BRKgSEFQNa36TYv0EZt8dkDK1-dT41BVVAOCYPHAzVtnO4TMRcSy1GrXIUP9iZWdtc8dBQrgq5_zGIY8VZfEhDLcvXEfV_aCjmBvYMBPp5ATXoVxY0WmHx4EfsBYCdy2tq47KHsrKKUz0k9oTY262_YNu86klBeIeBQ=> .

 

Everybody's Doing Multiscreen

 

Mixpo surveyed over 300 industry professionals for a study on how they are using multiscreen advertising. According to the report, "[in] 2012, 78% of agencies ran multiscreen campaigns in behalf of their brand clients, and 90% expect to run multiscreen campaigns in 2013. In contrast, 81% of media companies ran multiscreen campaigns in 2012 and 96% expect to run multiscreen campaigns this year." Read the report here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iq-B05jDa3q1yuPyhPfGuPVLtkXK8Sfw6Hk3ed8IqAAOmBJb6o_iiTSA-HUCCXmR8QOU7Ggeq6coi5AFHLYk6htsb7AZ_rnpucnM5OcPA6jCUFnr5XlNhA6QjM3DEGDn>  and the press release here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iq-B05jDa3oI8HfNojE7g6yVwY4z9YQMrDx-8ofoe0Ib84Q_1rVmhQsZoWIWFSub0PyLH65Gjq7WNgBJ3k9D-S8yJu4gIAqbuM3V4MmMVH7hjorQRO79IQlUf9UrPrA_xxRzxetmB3EdqAKPqGW1YpC-EjRAkYxvvNs40NZUeY8ssve2h2r0nIl-MOqna5zYCKlOlXZAmzGTZOwGTFfsjnVa2iCq2KdLQdoE-PcxekDQKWDYESS1FuERrxSORDm4QArECQ2v9i5DUsvo5RN8LQ==> .

 

Are Oreos News?

 

In a column for PandoDaily, Kirk Cheyfitz, founder of ad agency Story Worldwide, criticizes the idea of brand newsrooms. Given that brands are only interested in talking about their products, it's difficult to make them continually newsworthy for audiences. Cheyfitz pulls out three points that make newsrooms effective and potentially workable for brands. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iq-B05jDa3rRJcOPABOjO4otd29fo1Nhy9838ohHSw60NUjq9zM0ksv_3QLVLt_3fKGau7U_wlfG3CWvgQykAOubBlXGlZQRpuVXjMVtUIoomf56qe_7qJqRxFaHYQ1PQyE7fRGwtXQ_5om8M2VG1OonrmEjsGoQ2Ax24SHDE2PiGkDpNIcTceFbf3F_ycDB> .

 

iRadio Is Real

 

iRadio has officially been announced at Apple's Worldwide Developer's Conference, and it appears all the rumors that have been swirling are spot-on. The service will stream music to a user's device, supported by text and audio ads, accessing the iTunes music database to do so. Furthermore, users can create custom playlists or allow one to be created from their pre-existing library. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iq-B05jDa3oGgHuJVFIfI03F_lTY8XWMp8RVxg6N4FmyMsWFM9-DI4KM3ESzYsYe33oUbOlCesEWBieNvrQPzVRKf6XfYRYfMtZiexrsSxK6EVy4zx_ZQeE_owcLVrKxiKc15KTtrTl3FS_6R3IpUGjDFdVF_dbW> .

Finding The Waze?

 

After talks with Facebook fell through, Google may have swooped in and offered $1 billion+ to acquire social map startup Waze. According to Israel-based Haaretz, the move is a done deal and would keep Facebook from directly competing with Google in a very important area - mapping stuff. As part of the deal, Waze will reportedly keep its offices in Israel and team in place. Google is supposedly offering all cash, but no official comments have been made from either company. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZbDYfVFpZXYGefGxXVGnS6vZQGIGjLkKhv2USfrJY68bwVVECv4HFxqZa1Le0jUDbalgJc2r7n6g8f-feQXJcWLCDlak46mPGo-z3RtNtVs3rzggpLhTyeC1XTFsW5f98txtkQ_GIgjk-nYW4ewuOYAa-uxxgRyPdqA7p9Qz0vR-rl4p3EyUNG8ODrCV-fG8nrDWpCdB0dltuXsFekI9cpENGrYi7Rqmzmjjo-7J5Cg=> . Haaretz describes Waze as "a crowd-sourced, mobile-oriented navigation device for drivers that relies on information provided by its 47 million members to populate its maps." See Waze's site. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZbDYfVFpZXYNiWg5PRqiYIAqM34z7PKZjuYhwXBJhDqMc4sDcKffsbdazpUNszYbeMybKMZDvo3Be5kgCeZAB4aVPSsnyANMGx02SjpPOzLV5Drg7dgWxA==>  Implications for ads: more data points for location-based advertising through Google. Facebook will need to look elsewhere for more local data.

 

Programmatic Continents

 

Xaxis is opening offices in Latin America. The Wall Street Journal's Suzanne Vranica says that WPP's trading arm sees growing opportunity there - faster than the programmatic pace in the U.S. and Europe. One reason for the growth according to the WSJ: "[Brian] Lesser at Xaxis says Europe has very strict privacy laws. But in Brazil, for instance, there are already third party data companies operating so Xaxis anticipates a less-restrictive market." Read more (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZbDYfVFpZXaEPCfge22mTxQX4NIC4QEHhwO-BcfDzRyQCi-H9YUCK4dnG_xB78ij_S0h9xj937Oj2Ny-ynHCm-dMYjIHdRkAsbJAFNPIPpf3ObmD2H1cm2aC6BkjdsRtRLM8r8di2dgYbEvDvlK6xTf2HNB8mvm6zvaOFatUSJH_Wxl17TNGoXi6zoJo1XhH> 

 

VivaKi Gets Native

 

VivaKi has partnered with native advertising startup Nativo <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZbDYfVFpZXZINgSVJURx3B0sB4g2Jppk29AEFgiaJWGaf-gJkS7xwy_guR1iWwWKdF-SpDuIsnBvAgFKCuB1PRYeGNLe0vPgNMyD9nAmMQGH3pPyz2ohiA==>  (that's like calling yourself "AdExchanger" amidst the ad exchange buzz... oh wait... uh) demonstrating the increasing interest in native advertising. Michael Wiley, Managing Director of VivaKi Ventures, says in the press release that Nativo offers "publishers a turnkey solution for native content insertion at scale without losing the native look and feel that home grown approaches offer." Does that mean "premium" CPMs? Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZbDYfVFpZXbamb7HR4U6Yt8c3_9-GCxBAUyUag4rcfLnPXlKu-zkUWO-kdUBBSE8ZKYpJPz_rHZfW8tWWrF83SbRSE0Ocu6_W3flS3qLHjztMCH2gt73ue0T6l_aA62rS2c2lngG1BofJ2CKPoBXjoJlsRmsHhrA2C6akO-kisbm9AozRW5aPMOt7GAM8JfxZ01z8UIUcQA=>  Nativo announced a capital raise of $3.5 million in April <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZbDYfVFpZXaSH7VilLFkK67vky5bPj21CZfUyaMF9Cv0PEzO2zv34g39xejoHq5YvedBG-vppmKw5RNr1BI18E1kJBmHEE0xa3idKqCPPrmv_3OAJJlyvYjkxq3qMKaXAYVv8KgM0tVO0t8ecmsWxWUPGnGamPapLJQN8A03XrZhFU4G41crhiuuubzUL_7EooPHReQnO-4MYzaAdMYvT9CjvOCY3iEuy7H-KkwafZsBOrGrvyR4FQTxiGTGh4nPKiDUJ2crF9NIcZin84zIz1F8YNdRA1OQoKbHciEIOmx5DTgYqkW46p3PpfqPVA1OkKpmvD5hzWr_ow7YqZsFng==> .

 

Who Needs Cookies

 

Adam Markey, Senior Product Manager of DataXu, outlines the benefits of a cookie-less future in an article for Business Insider. Markey discusses three challenges facing the third-party cookie, such as the multi-channel nature of consumers and he outlines different replacements for the cookie that are currently being discussed. "So why is a cookie-less consumer a good thing? My favorite answer is that it enables us to think hard about marketing in the greater context of a multi-device consumer." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZbDYfVFpZXbn-Zuq-XiTQiVLWDvabTIRFUfAMtVPUzmzOv95H4U5YtwVsCxkqdABqp-CUqY0RMGYv-AxQ-VUSrm7EFYfL9sQZ9hMkc_4vOMKTKz5mTBTogUE8QXEeNUETvjHgoDQcr2vKHiZrSZCAm_kK9j1gC20nSAj-4miVrBYkV986ofKhY6w9JfEMWWZ> .

 

Momentum Release

 

CAPTCHA ad purveyor Solve Media plans on revenue of $13 million to $16 million this year ("net" or "gross" is unclear in the article), according to TechCrunch. "Soon we will release a mobile product that performs as well, from an effectiveness standpoint, as our desktop products," said CEO Ari Jacoby. Along with the revenue, Solve Media expects 4 billion ad "engagements" for the year. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZbDYfVFpZXZGEbUNEw60ULdxJ23FifOghezZfmB0VDdVMi3SYuU_QI1ObpIattP11fcmdBUAwatkK5LwwhVR3tcMtJaxHixp_VYxQOB2KcV0f9dBFG46yT5eV2VFADuel5lrG3O09LI7U736uhWRJVq6sDAmfdY_00VpM5KZ7gw=> . Solve is up to 50 employees according to LinkedIn. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZbDYfVFpZXbWM4dLK0fd_X3C8GeD9PYwHlYxPmNlwlWdc1rgYDeHDCO8oajsYMBXMN0BfpbO_lU813AFR-l8j7F8P0VsCZ7oeuTTvUriyBVuH7NDuxmCEUIPCSFPfBPUOQyDwhWGTbM=>

Privacy PRISM

 

Unless you were holed up in your Armageddon shelter over the weekend, it was hard to miss news of a major privacy story erupting as the U.S. government has been apparently asking tech companies to give up their consumer data, claiming it was in the interest of national security. Read more in The Washington Post. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZbDYfVFpZXZSK-VvrHTPzkKtOIVjb60tNJfLIjljnfFYnenYWsJh5XfAKYyHGhmy8VArehIg1cXBp3Rnvd1-KuE350D_2TGgB1wbB-9AGwVLXwG0I8XrDseozAEvT13YXbe0NYJODwcQA-H3UQ83tc3u2bJfDTcZlZitKRulwI5aEiryeItVGbBFZ22OJU9prREL379hTP4nMdjEUkLdE0kVRl9RVAwdmxClEhR7FejFFCdS1wWdG0qe8VSpwYJZtVrfbnw5YNE8b6WZJh0OIiodo_JK3f5kxvZXLDlsunmC-J_UzZwX6EqnGEwXxQRMD-g0MG7Op1ulM6rhPbb2dozOPWXemMF3FK-Nqx5CMC0=>  The initiative, known as PRISM , is unrelated to advertising, but there are echoes of concerns with the online behavioral ad business as "big data" and its insights are at the core of PRISM. More on the whistleblower from The Guardian. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZbDYfVFpZXbckLB4V4caHXUHx4778yUFNUTNaq53JDERU4rwp2YFznXBL97QZVPaZsdHo6gbStC0n5d9VQn6NGQna8ei6f6jOWIVCYXionSv7ktK5ZXMjHyu7dL9fCE9-ynQhCfrCSmKs0Hr5Gg9vAMKBJTzhDSrUaIzdCPSv-XySxdTKUo5J-QBEFIEqFmV3Lfm_x8LH9ih2FcLBIjXUQ==>

Standardizing Native

 

It's clear that IAB loves a good task force, and their latest effort revolves around standards and best practices for native advertising. See who's on  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FUDZ28E6nSR35YUClb1UklCsgl7YQCMlkurmMtaUTxoe_YJ-mXgApbQ77_p2R0hmBQKiy2wEjvLWkK9OF2zHhs6fm14JekhP-1KGoe--ofPTjxvV2ZizwtbYen_1k1vKuOTygbfnolnPiOkARBSb60UinyNH5bQrqCP69sylavMUk3-e6ANsSdhhaDQ9Bm2Q93OU-28PUvVMhmxm13K1ng==> "The Force." According to the IAB's blog, they are also launching a Content Marketing Task Force to be an umbrella or a cousin to the Native Advertising Task Force, which will "aim to establish a framework for the native advertising space by putting forth a prospectus that clearly lays out today's 'native' landscape." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FUDZ28E6nSQKfV0kkAl4bZMfRvQNrJpwavznX330VbF1NKIg_eyBWBOY8JRg9ois7S_o0eELNzghc4sMOZ2nOjdg042cu3H7ycPpUGdDxSyQ9WxXFtvrkvJNhXliNEkvvsMbOqAYCiTqWmtj3cEVOQF_oxGJhahKxEUITxKDtzA=> .

 

Mobile Ad Barometer

 

Bloomberg gets the Google mobile ad scoop in a interview with YouTube VP of Sales Lucas Watson. Lucas says YouTube has received at least $350 million in mobile ad revenue in the last six months: "About a quarter of YouTube's 1 billion global users now access the service via handheld devices, spurring an increase in promotional spending to reach that audience." No AdSense revenue share there - all Google. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FUDZ28E6nSSmFM5mblpoEY9uJf0Gi9A8mmFpne6c-isH6szfgpSMZepcBMqrAe6SgEah0D4Xf4RvGjgS20PsYwdAiBo387h-J7BoFCvBTBzm-LuX5SYIkS_PEkhJT_w_-CYhoYEtyLHWacGgPztNteS8J8xkct7GcoMaD4R1s2sF4y_CafEAApeq2OAZtvJFpNrwj88Jo98n5Bd9pOc_B2BnpWC2W2ZqPwZnGuMfPR4=> .

 

Momentum Release

 

At its European Summit yesterday, AppNexus gave a reading on the mobile buy-side initiative it announced in April <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FUDZ28E6nSSQUqzVARjfZXxMoEuQKy_pFdyVjkpxoB0yLQvvYDxtrMWxSM5ALs-lmWctaYxXjCBX4A1g1zZT0Fg-G9emgW8NaJV8mYsYzU3KJzKFofBIZ30N3t_K0Pxy35BUES0tkXB4niRDBeCMb0L7CQmGH04vV0LgFtXGpWauyT6eUl5wVM-sSmRATE5Hfz-IhGaC0c2CxUh9Lq91f1R1F7EW4kPE> . According to a press release, they have seen a "67% increase in mobile impression requests, a 3x growth in the number of mobile-sized creatives in its system, and more than 250% increase in mobile spend." SHIFTing Gears

 

SHIFT released an addition to its real-time marketing platform called SHIFT Media Manager, which they are calling the "next generation of SHIFT's legacy social advertising app, GraphEffect." The company boasts a Facebook Strategic PMD designation and access to the Twitter API. The new product includes a number of features like collaborative worksheets, a campaign builder and a global dashboard. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FUDZ28E6nSRIwlspjXU8-i8YIbNaKAfcw8nPs6qMHrUsYH4JaGWVP8pf8NeAv1n03Gtyu_ayhjtvv4kfWsQIfnN8UOnbTv-9YUtUKw6cjWDiUmXgtaLQTrymR1vCbnr97r7C4L-Jj-7N0_Je6qUvUtw7wPYn6WnQWfA8NeFi6qrE81s90LxBR9H_YDeDJBoT4CTtsDoCMAH9ccwsVi1_7nGdXra2RIX1uZUPewfyiVZ3ZSsQRZ0qrA==> .

 

Programmatic China

 

Chinese ad company Tencent launched a DSP called Tango and has a DMP in the works, according to ClickZ. The new DSP puts Tencent in competition with Google, especially in the programmatic space. According to the article and Simon He, Director of Product Management, "Tango's competitive advantage includes its bidding algorithm capabilities and the ability to leverage massive user data for audience profiling and targeting." Apple Vs. Android

 

There's more to the Apple vs. Android market share battle than meets the eye, according to mobile platform Flurry, which analyzed its own data on OS segmentation. Although Android is currently winning in device market share, Apple iOS users are spending more time with apps. Flurry speculates the reason there is no clear winner across the board is because the nature of the two systems is different; therefore, the users have different habits. Currently, Android is also bigger in the international market, but Apple continues developing new programs to get their phones to consumers around the world. Read what it all means <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FUDZ28E6nSStAAc3FCl4HpxCx1pelF4AaZ6wMgCscpV-gOSrkMJqTRCZpiMOsx3c5xTFibDhe1-V5ehP2R1krR-yrmF3gr-njEZqQFb2EAPFGiV6nyM8tuqUxTT7b8hLQfuM61VJRxsDH_XJghnF0pHaOyEy8CXB_WAsyuNcPo-rJPldcLjfmRlGHBJfvto4m49bMAMHh5qRqjR3X11YYtCEXGm9bDpq> .

 

Kids These Days

 

Doug Weaver explores "age" and digital ads in a column on Upstream Group's "The Drift" blog. He admits that things may not have necessarily been better in the past, but older generations look back with nostalgia on the "good ol' days." He writes, "Our age problem is not about youth; the energy and core-familiarity with technology, social tools and mobility that young executives bring to the table is priceless. No, our age problem might just sit with those of us in our late 40s and 50s who continue trying to retrofit today with the yesterday we remember liking a lot better." You know who you are... Third-Party Valuation

 

How much is your data worth? Merkle is launching a new product called Merkle's Digital Data Optimization Lab, which brings data valuation and optimization to CRM for its clients. Ozgur Dogan, SVP & GM of Merkle's Data Solutions Group, tells AdExchanger the announcement is more than just its data marketplace Brilig (acquired in 2012 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QW8dFAeQehDc-jds2jlvn3ch0bdwji6d-Ixz7z397472Ky2yq32Ii39WPFJcCR0c0p76x96xZ4ioJluokaM-_pcfl03Fy1gbcM1y93roMFrMeFb2MQH4t-bx1uSku5X3DC0FCVdxtIYKdkXFo4vkzFaIvG6sjpG5Z3-Ceiw9NJXj5pmsFeEjQrPREzbouSI2YlRev4JruQp5o_8tMZhx7lkZRQ5Y-JT9dklx-gqbqhb3WAVp_N7yAoD_opK1endCTts2NJTUfnw=> ) being formally integrated into Merkle's product offering. In answer to whether this is a data management platform (DMP), Dogan said, "This could be one of the solutions that powers a DMP, but our focus here was to look at all the different third-party data sources that are available in the marketplace and leveraging the first-party data we have access to - as well as our analytics - to determine the value of third-party data sources." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QW8dFAeQehDm7vPs01vlfp_Z9svYiq_bLcL_nqdcdVIGZrBll8xpUMgmuli4Y5jt5S5TCNQcqE5hXFp5KRn8VU1H9oVXzcFyywb5Zg4EfdqIJ7hDNQEf6qonItdBELuyqYIrQGzR6M922kpLMIaHCmbjVWDBI-bvLRPbF4U7g4Ifl3xW7kVabCcA1EqF9Avh-NcoVRxmJV69LMLjGGRR2EUdUNoordCGLV-bux6wq3pIPldop6l8pg==> .

 

Rating Online

 

Bernstein analyst Todd Juenger claims Nielsen is going to be the clear winner of the online measurement derby, in spite of comScore's efforts. MediaPost's David Goetzl quotes Juenger from a research note: "When faced with two multi-platform offerings (comScore and Nielsen), one of which is tied to the TV currency (Nielsen) - as long as the two products are reasonably comparable, we believe Nielsen will win." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QW8dFAeQehBS0WDRDFrnkbWpCun9iLioHY6F6e1lQcG1aQo46j6KOG_0HYg1gH6kdnXxN-NKUT_ZcOAYOxvpqs0tvtZrWxJNyO8b5k7xs8tsQwYAe4oE9idaJ7I-BdcgD142FsnjZlm8adhmJYcg_M8caF9hvjNtD3d-rp6lr6KVChkoabzyq8wu_VARb76-pKnM_qsUnqB1MUdRQrBG4sQTQ-U7Pu3Cj4gOe0JnPe8=> .

 

More iRadio Rumors

 

Apple will indeed be offering advertising on its yet-to-be-announced streaming music service, says Ad Age. The ads will be sold through iAds, and there will be an option to purchase each song directly from iTunes, according to the article. Nobody from Apple has commented on the new product yet, but they are expected to announce it at the Worldwide Developer's Conference. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QW8dFAeQehCojkm5d-8egdhoEiRh_sanL6kq6qVzkHbofGr2T4BkKRxTWp_nD7JMzSm3lf8Gxfafkl4MlINnf0iuSW54ckmZN9t1NsHmkDzmdC9D0NXiPnJ5PDl05g8tNqpdcZUPRxvVqHRIGejrQhr1URqpx2OmKngYahEqHWyIpFMnI8n0vM35-wXaKl_s0Phw1i1tifMWpLmOILZqzyqwpPW9ECxH> .

 

Search Is Display

 

Search results are getting more visual as Google told advertisers that you can add images to your ads for search engine results - called "image extensions." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QW8dFAeQehA1QZNw4bmXg6sWP3_EHakuHIeEq-0v_bdzcoOAKvgX1LdLI258wz3WFjPBLdSCXNKngFK2JHRTVl9vBPGEzH1uIoQ5nUYR9vQrQH2GHsGzK1Y3s8sLPezp3DNO1jCD0QURE215d0gScYSKyyurLLCL4czwE0_xcUyFiWd-0bK-LLe4FYym0F4Rm5AVAGS09F4=>  It is well-known that pictures next text ads helps drive click-throughs, and Google has already enabled images for Product Listing Ads, for example. Googler Awaneesh Verma explains on the Inside AdWords blog, "More than one in six searches on Google today provide results with visual content. Image extensions will show in some cases when we determine that a search is likely for visual content. For example, it is more likely that your image extensions will show for a query like luxury car designs than locations of nearby car dealerships."

 

The Video Of Mobile

 

Digital video is a hot topic in advertising, so it's no surprise that Google's YouTube tripled mobile sales in the past six months, according to a Bloomberg news article. Of course, the challenge is keeping consumers engaged enough to watch pre-roll ads on their mobile devices. "People have less patience on the phone; consumers have become more task-oriented. The ads have to be entertaining and there's a higher bar to some extent," said Julie Ask, an analyst at Forrester Research. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QW8dFAeQehDbY0DrFJPcIH4O-_XqqsyKZrsM1XXjuVRJEAhVsb8ajPvu7LD085rW9DI9Wrl3L7UbVTAobHHsQiKG3yJjFlreHb7B4fWahQ21ACRDAXJ7X8sap3QrdWS-R7jXiTMnBljI0ElaOpxtWp9G4_3mDOC-o0IXmAjrR8XeMqqCI6bLbaiez9C4eYmQmXvwkIkoH19Iy09hE5K83itqEaO0rHswzUln18nQNtY=> .

The Intent Of Mobile

 

The abacus continues to burn at PricewaterhouseCoopers. Followings its Q1 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QW8dFAeQehAxJZLzGTbaPnA5eYL1ozse4z0ZVaCKE6eK-cYtyR3Wx5EwTmcd-JP3n61vT9tlTa5YyhosTAqII3cMstcLdf3klagHWwo9U4Y6q5jOlOmVAhxA45DbSCScztbKUt8LJ08dO6ILaCYsw49GXMObh6sfx0f7WOrFEVf2YIhLeboca6oYWnD5t7cMTv9Vt2AjyZ-daa9M3xKbmB8zZoilFoSJjd41iLkQRjo=>  report with the IAB on digital ad spend, Multichannel News' Mike Farrell brings word of PwC's "Global Entertainment and Media Outlook 2013-2017." At an event in NYC yesterday, PwC partner Sean DeWinter said, "77% of Internet searches are done with a mobile device in the presence of a fixed PC or a laptop. People reach for their mobile device even before they look at the browser on their laptop," according to Farrell. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QW8dFAeQehCkbayU3TVaELLF1n3YZBmfnvXQe51j45ELwUoh7q5vNSNw0SrfVYoTeoDCjOXKkg_fXs1PRKfMpW4yTFjwK5haBXwG1QSjnZBr6SmA_k5y4OjED0ArhIzttM0Fp3eIciuCA1N1WKl8mMN4DSg2ASSMzGCWJzCphXwiqAxDWml5l3e8ohqx0s4sv4gKlFQ0pgHmxI34vsRmiQ==>  There's a lot of intent in mobile.

The Fruits Of Akamai

 

MediaMath formally launched Adroit Digital (see it) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_socZ5kQxMHFfWsvvQwbZUNwOM_r-NUbMfQPYsxoK1HEdrjAvFyK9kNjq6mvtkC9DZb6kv26fCo6fSAUK2glWT77PSIwxAGExZu2w8m9r_yr_aoKVxo5PegX3x-CDFjx>  on Tuesday, using the technology and the team it acquired <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_socZ5kQxMGyz4YD0Uh8LVilhGBXtytozq6V6rSOhpnKGMslzsAUXQYjdicT5Ot_P1ImT4n3Z0a9KfBdnbgGx4CwmRj4jdCYqPv8Lj7TkRAme_X9oPdc_nJYJcVbcWvCMVA1wyxP1gW3npNWcXdwZskXI-DUAYzHSrVOc0vSNLxs_z8CXL_EtA==>  from Akamai's ad business, known as Advertising Decisioning Solutions (ADS). It's also using part of the name of Adroit, the Boston-based dynamic creative optimization company it acquired in 2010 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_socZ5kQxMGQH7ImwVLrHUAVn41vjylS_1HNwowyPW8lrQtBhH0VGSIMj0J2fa6uMWLtZgFMUJkR8_dmz-u257V1w7iiFGEfGeuoFGLPiojvq7hhAbBMr8tnxU9_0sPhoJr6F4V9mHGJ7PIuWEdvXP-u7ESAxHQMUA43IgsVT2EM-SQRPI_8_wPh5ty2i82U9OV_t89DgCbzNW_p1thFjDebblV0t8JD> . The new business unit positions itself as providing access to the same data co-op that Akamai's ADS was built on, with more than 300 companies contributing. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_socZ5kQxMFhXCop9HOt_2zBO7M3EUn6yVeuCb9I9qU0Ue0144NArNuHBnZWBhJQ0OZu21ugI11uycUsP1rD-lEyR09IOaP9HDNw4NJ5wOm4QTDBjkxmrVO4DtRd3DAbOQu7wDWnvRRNHHCCfOWemuofRV_Abz2wDbJiCaaTV2xRfGxslaX3dr9H5rtAgQb1mESqhWaUEycLgpUwPMO4PvPD_Eo7rIibQYKqwP4jdpZ9i5_BwrDNQiW_pMhWJMbk>  and MediaPost <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_socZ5kQxMEgb-XgSp-rGhcOvOEBe8XvnmbbKlhNR1vuAQZak4ZhoEM3pNjGCnAzTDFt_AzwEs4xaX_qrWRiTRQTcq0EKcdTYHtiam2d7HWzp2fVTOY4OYB2RXHFOXzlpgHJ_nGE87dnncusEEwT508Goe8QSWbH3PxLaIBBvYSojRO9cqgQkbEOwNHtH7silVy5RPC2L7W9WCRnqsOzyfsRcqsKyu-uOEICwbaxzN0=> . MediaMath's managed services business is evolving too, as MediaMath CEO Joe Zawadzki told AdExchanger recently, "We're not providing managed services at MediaMath. When we bought ADS, the division from Akamai, we took the rest of the trading services team, the managed services team, and merged that with the ADS team, and that has become Adroit. They're another separate entity." Also bubbling: MediaMath's exclusive license of Akamai's pixel-free <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_socZ5kQxMEu4GJK5J7OVkVOBLkixmTdGYS_VAtrmfdwjwsnU3-2qD19Q1FRRm4lZ1smjyUoxvoa56vF8lgg9-yqyuRPVP6sc4bMoSa-tCGpzpO_1I5HUG2JjZkXhGD2Sr4fcxc3a-kVym1T6xS9Be3sQn15_-4zVomu_F0B9Brkthfi1k3eQfSRoZf0UDU1nOkmwD0AZIpot0PGcQVBaFnqrJhZX281oT3wPd90LgPVr_QoedbV6h30dSitLyZ3OLVvK3IZ3Ko=>  tech and access to the data co-op may not last forever, as Akamai could want to cash in and open it up to other platforms that wish to retarget co-op data.

 

Brand-Safe Headache

 

Recently, a group of advertisers had to temporarily pull advertising from Facebook because their ads were appearing adjacent to controversial content. Meanwhile, other sites like Twitter, Google's YouTube and LinkedIn claim they have measures in place to prevent the negative adjacency and, ultimately, the backlash that Facebook received. The NY Times Bits blog weighs in with marketer reaction: "It is up to the social companies to create an environment that provides that level of support and safety for the companies," said David Reuter, VP for Corporate Communications at Nissan Americas. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_socZ5kQxMFN_-lNHLT7W8PQYNqMl6s6cjj63VMYCGYU0yhbdems81_WaKuEyIL0cAr-KYrACas_fS-IhZwppgM175r_cZVQKbI_2B9dCYTbjOGF4450V0gVHc5SmyD_vOcGacv0NKxIci2nJ1vWUOcrNLAMQWrY2Oe4svgq-D2vuAM4pLw3-82tXrBqq4K9o05_QPUDl20MhTqKcbSxXOnPNBeyqdCF5QoC6pNRtOSD6n5qtseEEnGah3vFTDvFPiLvll_bZjxPiXBULpKMDw==> .

Daniel Rosen is taking over as new global CEO of WPP's mobile marketing agency Joule. WPP recently lost chief executive Michael Collins, who moved to Adelphic on May 30. Stack Refections

 

In spite of recent changes <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_socZ5kQxMHuKB1Z9iz41noiwycR6LYj_TRQPDC0lH07aLzTvVm1S-Oz8sIySpgLdlzxpT-CtRMGmX4nYEkhcH4Q8RywtxwKCSjNbpzZazdbHqjZkgfFD7iHbqHOQ4edZ8jUuel8ymJ2Ws4J6up1RjhJxNm2Sj_ioEx6Wwi2J8ENN4Cu1bHpPnJgzN5KU56lCJtnK9NYUiM=> , Publicis Vivaki's Audience On Demand exec Marco Bertozzi pulls no punches on his personal blog and reflects on additions to Google's marketing "stack," "...the real success has been where advertisers or whole agencies are swapping to [DoubleClick Search 3] and [DoubleClick For Advertiser] because they are or are about to be heavy users of [DoubleClick Bid Manager - was Invite Media] and want to benefit from the frictionless web. I work with people a year ago who were nowhere near wanting to work with DFA and were proudly using Mediamind or Flashtalking etc and have now switched and are happy." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_socZ5kQxMGxs4hHDip4QE3wokyKd3j4oftziWbirXGZO9tkPVkuW5uen9L1o37G86YHfg8urilqNQlKsv8kTJu0Q6BhVi4lCxLStoS5QCq9XnGV97ekD1yYxdB9coQU48CrPSdjwPsu1BmVYL991SlX1nXnQHLnn4uXOVOsQR1pxH3SqL8BNw==> 

 

Personalizing The Page

 

Webtrends, one of the not-Googles among web analytics providers, has beefed up its Optimize platform (a targeted landing page tool) with new features. Brands can now use in-session and behavioral visitor data to customize pages, as well as test targeted content, among other new functions. Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_socZ5kQxMG35w9CCa6VuZVD4-u4R02_ENSuDfiRa0RB9J629sjhW6ySemrDdZdITkDna-TKmBRH7yQoz2GuNX2KCLc5eWeLOnb_uZyc5k1NfZjL-agOywJcIz9a45dPCf12_MYijIvbB-K_kbIVevubpQ_t73yO99ABnCnlBpvwqzkKsmwR8llKFVlzW285pdfOnGtIZOMOI_bNh6lKZ-LAdZim3cEJ6GVn7qYo9HkG2CmASeh4tBmE4I7dxYGfW0CkGAL2frQ=>

Carving Ad Pie

 

On his personal blog, agency kbs+p's Darren Herman carves the digital ad spend pie from a variety of sources and finds that six companies are taking in 55% of online ad dollars. He notes, "Google's growth is terrific and Yahoo! took a step back in 2013. I'm always amazed to see Google dominating digital ad spend with 41% share whereas the next closest competitor is around 4%. That's 10x. 10x!" Read more; see the pie. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_socZ5kQxMGYXPe6BQGRmc6yR2alt5h1uFQvwHtBxNopvam1OPw8ZEkdiENi1yZkocBKJOiXU-5i18WiZCLVJC28nnq9990NWyGjnFV7GRelqz0f3BT3hYpiPRcNu1M95jsFXv_JXYlrSCbUnZid4WSVN-_cegEzhRpWQtUVUuc0U5mxBdyac85KXXeiAKrEoVNBLjfcU5dKlznxlwEjmAlypLXDCXYLloY9j4wm9CkNLh611BXLbw==>

Counting The Spend

 

Online ad revenue has hit a new high -- $9.6 billion -- according to an IAB and PwC report. That's a 15.6% increase in just one year. "This first quarter milestone clearly illustrates that marketers recognize that digital has become the go-to medium for all sorts of activities on all sorts of screens, at home, at the office and on-the-run," said IAB CEO and Prez Randall Rothenberg. Read the quarterly update <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qdg9uYneEC8K_tLF9FdwIVNoGO4VgWxNGz_OMVxkIU2ZX6zPcQdW-NGO7cuKzJjc32VLNpcKNyBB2bXIRDTgmzMqVMo4fS_Fo-jA22h3ckKy7uDC0zllrr_l4bayFAg6oFvgVUhvtlRkBlUDVTnngGTXdgD375XeQrHKOLh-5aJUHMcU9i_JCixfU7yHMIDflIcO98aZlblcGc8W4OCqAyN-1FK0opQM5rRBjTPhhvg=> .

 

Missing The Spend

 

FreeWheel CEO Doug Knopper tells AdWeek that online video purveyors may be unnecessarily missing out on ad spend. "The linear TV guys have the highest number of ads. They are highly monetizing their content. Digital pure players are the lowest. They are not monetizing it yet. It's almost like they have different business models," said Knopper. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qdg9uYneEC8H-ARAMkFCHhn-QNBiL7GtYb3MlLTgNxuasHhh6RyMQtWMqo947MXq_AF5yi0mHLIgmEbkodxiioCDhENVueoKxv4ii3E2aKHzBS9Qjf-kpCRwMCtTFsW_Vp16V_fsIKKtHQIIPB1tH7eYV-dg9CDdvPBl-sONeO9pS-iQtu6XQhldvnbRGlmGZ7ilcngHT8Y=> .

 

Programmatic As Savior

 

Down Under, the former Chief Interactive Officer of media agency Ikon, Ellie Rogers, told a Sydney media conference audience that programmatic signaled the "beginning of the beginning." According to AdNews, she said, "Automated platforms provided an opportunity for sales houses to reinvent themselves as 'real strategic partners who understand their clients' business' able to develop 'bespoke data-driven solutions.'" Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qdg9uYneEC_f2-Ud-HJIPzIx5_v6TZQn540Y9KpAgnz-JcanBaZM48ZFh7duF0r2vp6MEqlTS8Pvgn6ONsovzefOJYd53IEn2O3D-JxwatnouwIwEidIXQnLuO-TjlbOCaMiIPZdh2J27NYbuvS-17CniR0MRyOtWQVfCk_TDSD2IqEPkG1NO9kNxGl2eZnSZEAMaWY-yyw=> 

 

Mobile Pain

 

Fewer companies have been hit harder by the rapid consumer shift to mobile than Zynga. In an all-staff email about a new 18% headcount reduction, CEO Mark Pincus described the pain and the opportunity. "Mobile and touch screens are revolutionizing gaming. Our opportunity is to make mobile gaming truly social." But he said getting there will require lower overhead. Read Zynga's blog. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qdg9uYneEC8Qx9iRt601lKz6JqswZFCmRKMkVFA9vVBrD4Z2OB1tYJwXE-A7DszJjtTNMbrZCuSdD9SrKdu_kASi-usgWdGbfEfihpXBxaLJ5J_BGuEs9iktrjRChKXH6v8Qi55LekboOaaIbS0BrcII8jtzI3Hw>  Zynga has lowered guidance for 2013 revenue from ads and virtual products. Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qdg9uYneEC9H-ic_MucKo36w-eQUz3qwtpEFxk6AHH3amKEG-tUUxfFSeAn_MEeLi2taB2B5-xMHoc4uqVp072FpA84Mfj2nzQfHwVdyLLmnGMf_ZVO3le-0N9GGvPbeUBGxeiRzvqwvxCBp_V7xKog22NBy1NJfb7OlqiQGk1gBF12_emxOob7Z5XKPuGh4FVVMkY7hH6w=> 

 

iRadio On The Horizon?

 

Apple has reached a crucial agreement with Warner Music, suggesting it's closer to launching a streaming service called iRadio. CNET is reporting that Apple may unveil the new product at its Worldwide Developers Conference next week. There could also be an advertising element to the new service, as Apple may include radio ads the way other streaming music services do. Given the sheer number of iTunes users, this could mean a much larger audience for advertisers than services like Pandora offer. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qdg9uYneEC9X9jhfa8HTI6mhfTWrn36WbO0wTqm4r0CqzOc_OkL-NHavA9j30lmJRfIckEAl4gYJKmvXdeCe-bGDaE7KI0n6Siwjf35gTJ3_MEJmLOawk4VGeKKBSjKEeEqx7JKjWAw-_LDWKuGby2v_BjqCjOpQL-Y27328-xVMInyKH1yEtZ6375J611Y2RLt0G5rHBHq_D1a3rxWFrnkbDaZ3Iso_2LCRRfQnb13vr-27OObxBA==> . Perhaps Triton Digital <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qdg9uYneEC9GHjKCL2m0EUc52eiXTBjU2hZIWCbYd1TGVUxJO2oeqQbbRXlBXahfPR5_poR1xbo835e6CTUDp5tC5v6nc3yFytgaKLRanuIej0qx2Oaq2HmbuPt3NK3CYa_L9Sh7-iomLf8fXZjOp0ot2z3nvbuu3Dfc61KvYc-TAHprjhGT2kKILzoAXLf0ZjnmcCSdt9erx4uzo9Vo-V0ae94cEjLsoGADRMOrPCmPmghQtCkNxA==>  can get a slice of the business.

Native In Sheep's Clothing

 

Google's spam expert Matt Cutts issued a warning to marketers, via YouTube video, that they need to be careful with labeling native advertising. One of the most pertinent issues stems from Google's search engine ranking system, which necessitates proper tagging when the content is an ad so that it doesn't show up in the results looking like non-sponsored content. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qdg9uYneEC8oDgw87v-ubQxlMRcVyQcF7UWr-r6LRUAbDaSJtD4SE3mcFutojLdvv8gN73lVBvmBoJGqUFZ_-z4pdLkstQzBhNbuwvoF1iPgffYmYGaI4SVJB5c1ZsfDYmThHafstuWpIodI3KJpkwKzq0HV7uMcpXCZBaATNfyW77dfhrtRI2a8A0eXm_FaSvqowyT8tvLqtoq_byPgfgUK4CfqMf6WeYntPmfOxvaEaSR_xSSvqgNoKwAFJuUjWBIfQQLX4j8=> . Do I hear "Black Hat" Native, anyone?

 

The Unbearable Annoyance Of Display

 

Microsoft has announced the publication of new research which says that if you're an "annoying display ad", you're driving away business, so shame on you! Using a test and control method (described here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qdg9uYneEC9vZmQjTfi3exOMq8TYJVnc2gH8Nc5gl4D_hRg44x7C6LVnComTvr_p5Gmx9zGm83n-wuc8aBMhfLsA0z4c0vD_bg5t17u9QG8kfBmVHBSEErPpD2RM6escWgz999I8sWTTdVBkJn1dIr55UuuUMWAwJ69md8B2c0Nbql70upn9FDJQyVRAgZIGMEnw58G_KoiMtUx2x6DBuhdT3sfUBU10-_T443seSU8w95oCyaPdzA==> ) that helps define the characteristics of an "annoying display ad," researchers try to quantify the loss to publishers: "In the experiment, the authors found that they needed to pay people more than a dollar per thousand impressions to make up for the lost traffic caused by annoying ads, compared with showing innocuous ads or no ads at all." Read Microsoft display ad chief Jenn Creegan's intro <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qdg9uYneEC_hPrzeTZluE86NtB97KWZJMIpUW15RssHeDUMBQlKg1RVqFU_Xv0FrgP1EbebCklo7xLdrJo_mqiR3k-m1gW1xES20PZreqb6BlqAxGkH9uMlY6CBhwKWmWyXug-QAqwZ3Lu84-WwHBotOORdS38fVx1MH519FNaYkDV2neECUEcMj42l7nEegIrKgOxp0yQuDopetofCLDHPNYtMWxpOYm_x-y6fTra_qGC72KUwUo8OszH83zEVqv_35Q6WWv09lKqXOmMFQBw==> . And, download the research (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qdg9uYneEC_sJnNUcpOT6mp2QPOk2dyCpqTIi7eYlBfaqWitor52rA7Cdl3SMU7CIGCujYumdyQ4mefBiIQUlmOFafE7SUyvfg-0qxaxpHutwEdVZSuhxYlzY0b8rJ5GBBJDX0ygBnM76uCsMQkSn4LMp0hd37iikgoqFTQHfv93mQ7tLy3OOUgwyIAZlHIj> . It's a kum-by-yah ecosystem moment, too, as Google's Preston McAfee collaborates on the research with two Microsoft colleagues - Daniel Goldstein and Siddarth Suri. A Microsoft spokesperson says that the three of the researchers were former Yahoo's before they took different paths.

 

RTB 'Wild West'

 

Turn Chief Architect Emile Litvak pens a retrospective blog post about the excitement and lawlessness of RTB's formative years. "There were different approaches, ideas being explored (anyone remember browser-based first-price auctions?), no standards (we have OpenRTB now), but overall there was a feeling of moving rapidly in a new frontier." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qdg9uYneEC_uubG0M_OjcF13zFkhwinTMcF_QULYCp-AlmWgaaUIC1-GzcprZTuUd02HZRM9__YS5dB_UBetRJShD0vl5ohVIij_i8H5uoGh9tVFG6TVsIvvMvdp8Y6sfyAvu7ym9L6zufzNYLyb80yELhPubU39MiUJujF44uV1FYaidwfcdIO4VaUVnnZA>

Conflict Of Interest?

 

It's not an agency trading desk story, but agency-vendor conflict-of-interest is the theme of a Digiday article. Tremor's S-1 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018XkyNo_5wLL2PBQavSSdS3x92GgqowPD3C2zsifr2kfowBXUtwdIGs_upF2fRcz7BVlO6dRaZdDgwcpkTq2QssN2db9JpIfLOHdgBUot46RsaRvJVz5BKJQFGtxOefazKJvZymf1Wj6Szi02Wv7n1X4ZKwLm74_KrwWM5V-HtTZqeeReAkuwvpgvs8wOrwVKmx-i_6In0i8=>  outlines that Publicis Starcom Mediavest Group (SMG) exec Laura Desmond received $300k in 2012 share options as a member of Tremor's board while SMG was one of Tremor's largest 2012 clients pushing $18 million in spend through the company. "The conflict" could be that agencies and their executives potentially give preference to certain vendors that supersede client interests. Marshall claims a similar conflict-of-interest may exist between Videology and WPP's GroupM. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018XkyNo_5wLJbTB6Zbin9ntvaWVQ3ejOYNwoqPDgSDrPJsCnBp3QxzzrCwg2sekNehHfgx9eltBxrK0sRrI9M20EHYV8OyCc3c8DDlaGUwI5nMf0wqsJnD4DhDlTolZ9SUuDjyrzNyxriKxnsRgpLtGVXEAPeOKdtPRCdDOpjrb24CQxcIX0k1qRvAyJvIZTw> . If you look at the S-1, former <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018XkyNo_5wLL6LxSWMgjEokLbGqQSXR1MJfGAWjBnioT7YUcJq5r4KC-tLsKHy-E2DBR89e5OF_6DDuiGWas4mxT11m0POCpkpp8YGCiq2FZG8G4bR71rxn7fLdd3NaOalFLH8LBNsYkzXg00YWguzCtFomCxlfaPHpaXbYK03oyVV-luucdWVYOWvMHeCnNMCcu4aI_FRji5r5tpCQU7Yw==>  AKQA COO Jim Rossman is also part of Tremor's board, but AKQA spent little with Tremor in comparison. The Desmond involvement was originally spotted by Stuart Smith <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018XkyNo_5wLLb-GUwx0cdtaTokiMDtr-GiAlKRzw5FegxVeK7SkIT3oQKJ4NsXmR_cixEdulG-s9Yyjrxw2GELtT-u9P-DoPNO_Cz_Ey_n4pHM8iCHipC8VCXOFQwMXjBnStz_D2svnFC-X6wi9WVfZEyhQUS-gn0LaT24T1H5bYelVTEcPjHmItF3L2c1zrnjrLx6dFGyLJaSksBHtLXFOy8HEm9_hPLhKKSZssqwaRmaSLciDNh_w==>  who suggests that Desmond could make upwards of $3 million if Tremor IPO's as expected.

 

Publisher RTB Adoption

 

In a Nieman Journalism Lab post, Ken Doctor explores ways publishers can survive if not thrive in the face of the apparent digital domination by companies like Facebook and Google. He sees private exchanges providing a glimmer of hope: "Such private exchange testing follows the adoption of RTB (real-time-bidding), which publishers are honing to get better rates for the ad inventory they can't sell locally. 'We moved away from a remnant inventory model a few years ago with the adoption of RTB and actively manage all of the programmatic demand that we see through the ad exchanges,' says Jeff Griffing, the Star Tribune's CRO." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018XkyNo_5wLKuUjLVPJG_m1beqRIys1mYt_VQZj7YvIR8O2w5zZvsE7MUS8k3zbUl5zUgqv_8t3iDz8WaZxJOyY3jTaZRqK-OoI80OxN15feb7Z9IIU3TV3MnrPxNuciyBc2UPREvLQMqCaAzERknQgzk5RCXVtLnuNedkUnqQpnrSUoV-I7tfbQtl-arJZzJsHJMysoxPH0=> .

 

Mobile Momentum Release

 

Mopub provided the momentum release du jour on Friday saying that it's marketplace has achieved a "$100 million annual revenue run rate this month." That's probably media spend running through their system as opposed to net revenue to the company. Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018XkyNo_5wLLTdUqdBX-BhoRFBj-PzVpmJTdl70gLYjJ1w20arE5lBuBFPZC6Yu8iPj8SHp5vmA0d0_gzlgCqUsIsrodbuzqmuY_xkJtRppWaPustaKO6LaB02Rwa2z9mB7sCoyXshtBWp2zQ7b0aUS4di7XFRFl87IXVlAHmg2CFshSg5-yb_3iqUY3qJoFbd-Yk29ycatCeIPGv0Pi3TA==>  A TechCrunch commenter notes in another article <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018XkyNo_5wLJ8kDE51k2z6_XGe0aVpNKNWwY67K2iV2se1fFI8AH2WqYmdbZzsi7OVvagPpokYPwi7EjK_mDkConenQ82-6E8ivRizvJpD0_yD6wotux0qjse1cC517_VUBv8sMKFERF3LMlKyFego2weAJxu3Z17KFA39MizdGCjITcWIriF-A==>  on the Mopub news saying that eBay enables over $100 billion in gross sales, but $3 billion in net revenue. Regardless, it suggests that display ad revenue is starting to see scale in the mobile space - and not just Google and Facebook. MoPub CEO Jim Payne says as much on TechCrunch <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018XkyNo_5wLJ8kDE51k2z6_XGe0aVpNKNWwY67K2iV2se1fFI8AH2WqYmdbZzsi7OVvagPpokYPwi7EjK_mDkConenQ82-6E8ivRizvJpD0_yD6wotux0qjse1cC517_VUBv8sMKFERF3LMlKyFego2weAJxu3Z17KFA39MizdGCjITcWIriF-A==> .

 

Buying Mobile Bulk

 

Mondelez struck a "mobile-only media deal" with Google, and brokered by Publicis' SMG, to help brands maximize their mobile advertising possibilities, according to Ad Age. "We've been urging mobile readiness at Google for three-plus plus years, and this year has been the year where it seems like the light has gone off over most marketers' heads," said Eileen Naughton, sales VP at Google. Mondelez aims to spend 10% of its marketing budget on mobile. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018XkyNo_5wLIaiVhZyvBzl6CzHAwaeEPVOowK5oLEJ8nK8SPnuNtD86mPvEI9RGBpAFTWxIum6_U0_Gg-o8jjeXZ1wxu8H6fgZbFsk4MG4mgDIyh_7_txRi0OCcTBv1t2FNc7Bmdhn1GIRO6SKTSAAzLB473ahmI0Z1w5DO6DVKy3SoVKT5c_rwjk414DPmJEGaUpbSUYfaW_CB53qN3FLw==> .

 

TV-Online Goal Posts

 

Rob Hof covers last week's RampUp conference in Forbes and reports that Google display chief Neal Mohan has a goal in mind for how to make TV ad dollars move online: "If we can prove digital costs half as much or has twice the effectiveness that's what brand people need to justify changing what they're doing." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018XkyNo_5wLJl_dJG9QvZawcsuHhmSK6XA7Kdu1vdUZHhetBe2OYlFJKhoCEFZYpBAyFePvCJgR1taLregrtl0Q6gEmAOTNeHXY6H8mRGCBxgMiA7tLKxsgDTMKk9zrH1PfsNrdvom4IXS4UclpzPQ6vfgrTEPdoCES0DUm5YlLZXWYuuPuj_kvwEF2kCdNxBtKfEsFor7mWNkuPnspkdx4ji5ZmeAsU6fLBrqHeDJFtwfZBkgYbkIQSSkKSoU2AnIK4F5uHUIgU=>

Ad Network Heading South

 

According to Reuters, Millennial Media CEO Paul Palmieri said the company is looking to expand in South America, where the mobile market is apparently growing rapidly. "Mexico and Brazil each have such a substantial number of smartphones that it's absolutely exploding down there. And the percentage of smartphone penetration in Argentina is hot," Palmieri said. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018XkyNo_5wLK_ffwLHMQkSgFjA4ujGACRq1h60Y95PQhu1VWN0zlf4QU9qD2QY6EHZRtaD4D-xkEdHZBv6eGzLqQ3Aan5fMoIT2JK5STh3epMDgLZDxFwt80yD4am5sUTKKCWInsK17ritorWkAx3p3mdhd5q93_YTk0JNDH8GjNh0tZGccDCL91QZCZsN4wfSZZ_cjc6SPYQoTSlTRUCAQmBobeRDiyz> .

 

Big Data Myths

 

Kate Crawford of Microsoft discussed six myths of big data at a conference, which were then outlined in a NY Times Bits blog post. Some of her points include the need for data to have context, and for people to have a choice about their data being collected. "We need to think about how we will navigate these systems. Not just individually, but as a society," said Crawford. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018XkyNo_5wLLAb7BYcunt-GWMRGWIdricE0wkLMMPrhc_9gP8haK4cv60HsXddlma2b-67_ZjZBii1kPr-_o3RE5Y_KMn9cUwJ_7rFH-SR2DGM1QqxoCesvbIzOfJQn77kYZcdTcDkR0n5a6JENzK_-PjGgtTVlVvV_2ZpZpDk9rgrBhJYpOpL5Y_hivB6kpg> .

 

Moneyball VC

 

Marketers are not the only ones trying to get their arms around "big data." VCs have started data mining to find the best entrepreneurs in the business instead of waiting for companies to come to them. "It's really about matching data with insight. You start and end with a qualitative thesis and decision but data can support or invalidate this thesis," John Lilly, CEO of Mozilla said. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018XkyNo_5wLKecJSoNsZBVaKQc9eDx1xWzRLVa1BQAd4N51oY2sW5TjdAXOmKftzY9S1KCMDyriwAxW8GiXAmqUSoRAB602hB3xpb-FWngPyDo0cJzyd-8HDOKi-xYmV_ps_bZjcu6L6uw2zZNui5xApI7t45xBVDJ7vjTxtv_8c=> .
